Your Colony Crew

Civvies
Civvies do not appear on your roster but may 
show up during missions. If you are short on 
people, you may also opt to bring along civvies 
to fill any missing positions. 
Civvies have the basic profile on page 18 and 
have no special abilities. They can only use 
Civilian weapons.
They do not progress in campaign experience, 
and the same civvy will not typically participate 
in multiple missions (though for narrative 
purposes you might decide that, for example, 
the newly recruited trooper was actually a 
civvy from a prior mission who has now 
undergone basic training).

Your Colony Crew

Stalker
A rare gene-mod, the Stalker physically 
resembles an ordinary Human except for the 
blue coloration of their skin.
Stalkers have no adjustments to their profile, 
but receive the following characteristic:
◆	 Shift!: Instead of moving normally, the 

Stalker may conduct a short-range teleport. 
Roll 1D6 and position the figure anywhere 
within this distance in inches. This is not 
regular movement, and the figure can shift 
through terrain and other figures. They may 
still take a normal action.

Sec-Ops are developing plans to dissuade 
existing colonists from following the same 
course, but a more wide-ranging plan is needed 
to deal with the risk to ongoing operations.
Sec-Ops refer to all of the above as “Tactical 
Enemies”: humanoid foes that use technology 
and function in a similar manner to standard 
opponents. Success for any colony will require 
engaging these foes in open combat and 
eventually knocking out their Strongpoints to 
eliminate their presence. We are recommending 
colony administrators treat security as a priority 
during their expansion phase.”

Campaign Turn Sequence
The campaign game is played as a series 
of turns. Each of these is divided into the BATTLE STEPS
following steps, which you must progress 7.	 Lock and Load
through in order. While the number of steps 
may appear daunting at first, at its heart, each 8.	 Play out your Mission
turn is a tactical mission with pre-battle and 
post-battle stages. POST-BATTLE STEPS

9.	 Injuries
PRE-BATTLE STEPS 10.	 Experience progression

1.	 Recovery 11.	 Colony Morale adjustments
2.	 Repairs 12.	 Track Enemy Information and Mission Data
3.	 Scout reports 13.	 Replacement Phase
4.	 Enemy Actions 14.	 Research Phase
5.	 Colony events 15.	 Building Phase
6.	 Mission determination 16.	 Colony Integrity Phase

17.	 Character event
Sick Bay 18.	 Update rosters

Injury table

D100 INJURY DESCRIPTION

01-20 Dead The character is gone. 
21-30 Seriously wounded The character must recover for 5 campaign turns.
31-45 Moderately wounded The character must recover for 4 campaign turns.
46-60 Lightly wounded The character must recover for 2 campaign turns.
61-95 Okay The character is okay.

96-00 School of hard knocks The character is okay and gains +1 XP as they reflect 
on their experiences.

D100 ROLEPLAY EVENT

01-05 The character is adapting to colony life and changes some of their habits.
The character spends some long hours at work finishing a project. Roll D6:

06-10 1:	 It ultimately doesn’t work.
2-4:	 It succeeds according to plan.
5-6:	 It succeeds extremely well.

11-15 The character makes a detailed plan for what they will do after their tour of duty or contract ends.
16-20 The character changes their opinion on something.

The character receives a letter from home. Roll D6: 
1:	 Bad news

21-25 2-3:	 General life updates
4-5:	 Heartwarming news
6:	 Great news

26-30 The character spends a few days in a bit of a funk about life.
31-35 The character pays another character a visit.

The character gets in an argument with another character. Roll D6:
1:	 Their relationship worsens.

36-40 2:	 It remains unresolved.
3-4:	 It gets resolved.
5:	 Another character resolves it for them.
6:	 It strengthens their relationship.

41-45 Two characters run into each other in the street and spend some time talking.
46-50 Another character gets the character a gift.
51-55 The character decides to pursue a new interest or hobby.
56-60 The character takes a few days of R&R.

The character goes out for a night on the town with two other characters. Roll D6:

61-65 1:	 They end up getting in trouble.
2-4:	 They have a fine night.
5-6:	 They get completely wasted.

66-70 The character makes a fool of themselves at work.
71-75 The character arranges a movie night with two other characters.

The character is assigned to a special work project with another character. Roll D6:

76-80 1:	 They bicker.
2-5:	 They work together well.
6:	 It strengthens their relationship.

81-85 The character has a heart-to-heart talk with another character.
86-90 The character finds a new passion in life such as music or literature.
91-95 The character begins writing a book about their experiences. 
96-00 The character goes out for lunch or dinner with another character.

Hazards
During its lifetime, a colony will have to 
weather many challenges and dangers.  
These may result in the colony being destroyed 
or abandoned, while others may inflict long-

lasting damage or change the nature of the 
colony in response to events.

The more common risks are:

Natural / Cosmic Disasters

terraforming technology allows

geologically safe, a wide range of disasters 

can strike, especially when a planet exhibits 
unexpected natural phenomena. These can

Research Basics The Research Process
To succeed on a new world, you will need new Conducting Research is done through 
and improved technologies, weapons, and Research Points (RP). Your colony receives 
tools. Many of these will be based on local 1 RP per campaign turn by default. Various 
conditions, problems, and available materials. factors will grant additional points or increase 
We call this process Research in game terms. the rate per turn.
In the Research step of the campaign turn, All RP earned are tallied up and added to any 
you can pursue scientific advances. There are you have currently accumulated. You may then 
three types: spend RP to “buy” advances. You can spend RP 

on multiple items in the same campaign turn.

D6 BIO-ANALYSIS DESCRIPTION

1 Hit bonus Analysis of evasive measures improves hit rates. 
All ranged attacks against the Lifeform receive +1 to hit.

2 Brawling bonus Development of close quarter techniques. 
All brawling combat against the Lifeform receives +1 to the roll.

Knowledge of vulnerable locations. 
3 Critical hits If both the hit and damage roll is a natural 6, the creature is slain 

regardless of KP, Saving Throws, or other defenses.
Improved understanding of weak points. Reduce any Saving Throws the 

4 Defensive reduction creature has by 1 step. If the creature does not have a Saving Throw, 
treat as a +1 Hit Bonus to all attacks against the creature.

5 Defensive bonus Better understanding of the attack forms of the creature. All characters 
receive a 6+ Saving Throw against all attacks from the Lifeform.

6 Predictive movement You understand how the creature moves and can anticipate it in combat. 
Reduce the movement speed of the Lifeform by 1”.

Educating young colonists to be scientists is an investment in the long-term

Earn +1 Research Point every campaign turn.

shield installation Local building materials provide increased resilience.

manufacturing plant Locally adapted weapons and hardware require specialized 
manufacturing techniques.

center Additional sick beds combined with newly developed medical remedies 
will increase recovery from trauma.

AI-assisted school 6 BP AI Theories
Much rote learning can be handled by AI-enhanced virtual teachers.

All new characters enter the campaign with 2 XP. 
Biological adaptation 10 BP High Level Adaptation

research site Your team is now capable of matching local genetic material to potential 
augmentation paths.

Receive 2 Augmentation Points (see page 105).
Bot maintenance bay 4 BP AI Theories

Dedicated bot repair facilities greatly improve readiness.

Repaired bots can now be deployed during the same campaign turn.
Civilian market 4 BP –

Availability of local and off-world consumer goods help the colonists feel like 
this is a real home and not just an outpost.

Gain 1 Story Point.
Colony shield network 8 BP Non-Linear Physics

Large scale power shields are resource intensive but directed partial shields 
can be deployed as needed, to anticipate incoming threats.

You may mitigate 1 Colony Damage each time you receive Colony Damage. 
Note that some sources will state the damage cannot be mitigated.

Cybernetic augmentation helps to achieve greater biological adaptation.

Receive 1 Augmentation Point (see page 105)
Damage containment 4 BP Advanced Manufacturing

center Allows coordination of repair and emergency maintenance crews to minimize 
the effects of colony damage.

Your colony repair rate is increased by +1.

AI controlled sentry turrets for point defense.

Gain 1 point of Colony Defenses.
Early warning system 4 BP Military Doctrine

A comprehensive sensor system to alert security forces of possible attacks.

Gain 1 point of Colony Defenses.

facility The default colony environmental systems are adequate but can hardly be said 
to be comfortable. Improved systems ensure pleasant temperatures and 

humidity levels at all times.

Gain 1 Story Point. Increase Colony Morale by +2.

Additional housing and life support allows for more staff.

You may expand your character roster by 2.

system Safeguarding the temperature, hydration and emergency 
food supply systems is vital.

Increase Colony Integrity by +2.

100



Colonies

BUILDING BUILD POINTS PREREQUISITES

Med-Evac shuttle facility 4 BP Military Doctrine
 Drone shuttles allow critical cases to be returned to a medical facility from the field.

Once per campaign turn, when a character becomes a casualty in battle you 
may opt to have them MedEvac’ed. After the battle they will roll twice on the 

injury table, picking the better result.
You must make this decision at the point a figure becomes a casualty; you cannot 

wait and decide later.
Military barracks 8 BP Military Doctrine

Upgraded training facilities for the security forces.

All current and future troopers gain 3 XP immediately.
Military training facility 5 BP –

Colony life is dangerous and regular refresher training is vital to keep 
personnel safe and secure.

When doing the Experience Progression campaign step, you may have any one 
character conduct military training to earn +1 XP. This can be combined with any 

mission experience, but characters cannot train while in Sick Bay.
Militia training camp 4 BP –

To improve security and safety, a colonial militia can be formed 
to patrol the perimeter.

Any civvies brought on a mission will have Reactions 2.

the environment.

Improved facilities for the development of advanced scientific principles.

With resources in short supply, the processing and recycling must be 
as efficient as possible.

+1 Raw Materials.

 Satellite coverage allows for improved long range resource scans.

Explored, add +1 when they are.

Every planet selected for exploration has its If the roll on the Campaign Condition table 
own unique environments and phenomena indicates an entry that has been filled out, you 
that the field teams must contend with. We receive the same Condition again, including 
refer to these as Campaign Conditions (or any secondary rolls. 
simply Conditions). Although you generate 
Conditions as part of mission briefings, you Unless stated otherwise, battlefield conditions 
should track these local peculiarities as part of apply to the enemy as well as your own troops.
the ongoing campaign game.

Campaign Condition table
When you begin the campaign, you will have 
a Campaign Condition table with 10 blank D100 NO. CONDITION

entries on it. Every time a mission instructs 01-15 1 
you to determine a Condition, roll D100 and 16-30 2 
consult the table. 

31-42 3 
If the roll indicated a blank entry, roll on the 
Master Condition table below, and follow the 43-52 4 
instructions (some entries require additional 53-62 5 
rolls). Write the Condition you have generated 
into the spot on the Campaign Condition table 63-72 6 
exactly as you rolled it. Going forward, that 73-82 7 
result will always be what is written on your 83-90 8 
Campaign Condition table. 

91-95 9 
96-00 10 

Note on Variety
The same Conditions can be added to your 
Campaign Conditions table more than once. You 
can either accept this as a common occurrence 
on your particular world or you can treat the 
second roll as No Condition. 

110



Missions

Master Condition table

D100 RESULT DESCRIPTION

01-08 Visibility limits Your vision is limited due to impenetrable darkness, fog, psionic 
interference, or visual distortions. This seems to defeat all conventional 
technological solutions. 
The visibility limit is the maximum range at which you can fire on 
targets or carry out any other tasks that requires visibility. Research can 
improve this limit. 
Roll D100 again:
01-30	 V ariable by round: Roll 1D6+8 at the beginning of the  

game and again at the end of each battle round to determine 
the limit in inches next round.

31-70	 Fixed: The limit is 1D6+8”. Roll once to determine what it  
will be in every instance this condition applies.

71-00	 V ariable by battle: When setting up a battle, roll 1D6+8 
to determine the visibility limit for this battle.

09-13 Shooting penalties Your ability to track and shoot targets is affected by a natural 
phenomenon such as psionic disturbances, malfunction due to 
background “haywire signals”, clouds of gas, or similar. 
A -1 penalty applies to all ranged attacks in certain circumstances.  
Roll D100 to determine those circumstances:
01-35	 R andom by round: Each battle round roll 1D6; on 5-6,  

the penalty applies that round.
36-65	 Range: All attacks over 15” range are penalized.
66-00	 C ertain terrain types: When setting up, randomly pick a 

terrain feature. All features of the same broad type (plants, 
rocks, water, etc.) apply the penalty to any shot that originates 
from, targets inside, or passes through the feature.

14-19 Movement penalty Due to gravity distortion, slippery surfaces, crumbling ground material, 
or grasping plants, you are unable to Dash under certain circumstances. 
Roll D100:
01-25	 T able surface: Anywhere on the table surface that is not a 

terrain feature. Figures in or on terrain features are not affected.
26-60	 Terrain features: Anywhere that is in or on a terrain feature.
61-80	 Climbing: While climbing up or down things.
81-00	 Crossing obstacles: When crossing any kind of obstacle.

111



Missions

D100 RESULT DESCRIPTION

20-25 Uncertain terrain Long range scans are particularly unreliable here.
features If you use the Uncertain Terrain Features optional rule (see page 137), 

add 1 additional Uncertain feature. If you do not use this rule, this 
result is instead treated as “Unstable Terrain,” below.

26-30 Unstable terrain Many seemingly solid features seem extremely unstable, and the 
slightest noise could collapse them.
When setting up, randomly select a terrain feature. All features of 
the same general type (rock, plant, etc.) are unstable. Each time a  
figure moves adjacent to or on the feature, or is fired upon while on  
the feature, roll 1D6. On a 1, the feature collapses and is removed 
from the table. Any figures that were in or on the feature will be 
knocked Sprawling.

31-35 Shifting terrain At the end of each battle round, randomly select a terrain feature and 
then move it 1D6” in a random direction. Features can move off the 
table, in which case they are simply gone. Figures in or on the feature 
move with it but must each roll 4+ on 1D6 or be knocked Sprawling 
(see page 38). 
Features will stop if they would otherwise collide with each other.

36-41 Hazardous Randomly select two terrain features which become Impassable.
environment

42-49 Resource rich If you win the mission, roll one additional time on the Post Mission 
Find table.
This roll CAN be a duplicate of a result you obtained from any rolls 
normally awarded by a mission.

50-55 Heavy scanner signals If the mission uses Contacts, place one additional Contact marker 
initially. This has no other effect.

56-61 Unusual activity levels The area is particularly hostile or relaxed. If using Contacts, 
roll D100 again.
01-55	 Modify the Aggression die by +1 when testing for Contacts.
56-00	 Modify the Aggression die by -1 when testing for Contacts.
This has no other effect.

62-68 Enemy activity The area is heavily patrolled, or the enemy is not here in great numbers.
This affects the enemy number encountered when fighting Tactical 
Enemies. Roll D100 again:
01-45	 Encounter sizes reduced by 1.
46-00	 Encounter sizes increased by 1.

112



Missions

D100 RESULT DESCRIPTION

69-75 Drifting clouds Great clouds of gas, vapor, or pollen drift through the area.
When setting up the battle, place three cloud markers 6” from the 
center of the table in random directions. Each produces a 2” radius 
cloud. These clouds cannot be fired through. Figures within a cloud  
can fire and be fired upon but it counts as cover. 
At the end of each round, roll 1D6” and a random direction. Every cloud 
drifts the same distance and direction.
When first generating this condition, roll D100 again:
01-70	 Safe: The clouds interfere with visibility, but are not dangerous.
71-85	 T oxic: Each battle, roll two D6 and pick the highest of the 

results to determine the toxin level. Any non-Lifeform figure 
that makes base contact with a toxic cloud at any point must 
roll 1D6 and on a roll equal to or above the toxin level, they 
become a Casualty / lose 1 KP.

86-00	 Corrosive: Anyone that activates within a cloud takes a hit  
with +0 to the damage roll.

76-82 Clear escape paths Once per battle round, you may select any one character that escapes 
the battle just as if they had moved off a battlefield edge.

83-90 Confined spaces Randomly select two points on the battlefield edge when you set up 
terrain. The table can only be entered or exited at these two points.

91-00 No Conditions All clear! No special conditions apply.

130



Missions

Delve Trap table

D100 DELVE 
TRAP EFFECTS

01-08 Turret Place something to indicate a gun turret where the Delve Hazard was. 
At the end of each Enemy Phase it fires at the closest visible non-Sleeper, 

non-bot figure. Roll to hit with +0 Combat Skill. 
It strikes with +0 Damage but negates Saving Throws. 

The turret can be knocked out. Attackers must roll a 6 to hit with ranged attacks 
or a 5+ with a Melee attack (add Combat Skill to the roll normally).  

A damage roll of 4+ destroys the turret.
A scientist moving into base contact can shut down the turret by rolling 

4+ on a Savvy test.
09-19 Paralysis The character that revealed the Delve Hazard cannot move or take any actions 

when next activated. They may roll 1D6+Toughness with a score of 8+ shaking 
off the paralysis. Scouts may roll twice and take the best die result. 

20-30 Blockage The area within 1” of the Delve Hazard becomes Impassable. A scout may move 
into base contact to remove the Blockage by rolling 5+ on a Savvy test. 

31-40 Laser beam The character that revealed the Delve Hazard takes a weapons hit with  
+0 Damage.

41-46 Explosive trap Every character within 3” of the Delve Hazard takes a weapons hit with  
+0 damage. If there is partial cover between a character and the Hazard,  

a 4+ roll on 1D6 is required to score a hit.
47-60 Sleepers! Randomly place 2 Sleepers within 6” of the Hazard. 

They do not activate this round. 
61-68 Alarm Until the alarm is shut down, a Sleeper arrives at the center of a random 

battlefield edge each future Enemy Phase. Shutting down the alarm requires 
moving into base contact with the Delve Hazard and rolling 6+ on a Savvy test.

69-80 Gas Everyone within 1” of the Delve Hazard is affected by the gas. 
At the start of the Enemy Phase in the next battle round, the gas expands to 

2” radius and then 3” radius during the following battle round.
Affected characters must roll 5+ to avoid being overcome. Scouts may add +1 

to the roll. Overcome characters will move in a random direction when they next 
activate and cannot take any actions. If an overcome character finishes their 

move outside the gas cloud, they must roll 3+ to recover (+1 bonus for scouts). 
81-92 Security Place one additional Delve Hazard marker in the center of the table and one 

systems at the center of a random battlefield edge. 
93-00 Lock-down One of the Delve Device (determined randomly) is locked down. 

To unlock it, you must make base contact with it and roll 6+ on a Savvy test. 
Once successful, you can then roll on the normal Delve Device table to 

determine how to activate it. A natural 1 on the unlock roll spawns a Sleeper 
at the center of a random battlefield edge. 

131



Missions

Environmental Hazard table

D100 ENVIRONMENTAL 
HAZARD EFFECTS

01-15 Confused signal A random Delve Device is moved 1D6+2” in a random 
direction. Reroll if it would be off the table. 

16-24 High security The area within 4” and Line of Sight of the Delve Hazard becomes 
high security. Any non-Sleeper figure that is within this area at 

any point of their activation must make a D6 roll.  
On 6, a Sleeper is placed at the nearest battlefield edge point. 

The status continues for the rest of the mission.
25-39 Unstable Area The area within 3” of the Delve Hazard is unstable 

(even if not in Line of Sight of the marker). Any figure moving 
through this area or firing a weapon into, out of, or through the 
area must roll 1D6. On 6, the area partially collapses. All figures 

in the area take a Damage +0 hit and the ground is Difficult  
for the rest of the mission. A second collapse makes it  

Impassable and causes all in the area to become casualties. 
Scouts can move through an unstable area without risk but 

must roll if they begin or end a move in the area.
40-50 Shock discharge Place a marker where the Delve Hazard was. Immediately and at 

the start of each Enemy Phase, roll 1D6. All characters within that 
distance in inches, regardless of intervening terrain, are unable 
to move or take any actions when next activated. Sleepers and 

bots also take a +0 Damage hit, ignoring Saving Throws. 
A roll of 6 for the distance ends the Shock discharge.

51-67 Toxic fog The fog expands 2” in every direction (blocked by solid walls) 
and moves at the end of each Enemy Phase 1D6” in a random 
direction, moving along walls if it would otherwise be stopped. 

Any non-Sleeper/bot character touched by the fog takes a  
+1 Damage hit, ignoring Saving Throws.  

Scouts are hit for +0 Damage instead.
68-79 Sleeper reset All Sleepers on the table are unable to activate in the next  

Enemy Phase. At the end of that Phase, place an additional 
Sleeper in the center of two random battlefield edges. 

80-88 Collapse The marker is replaced with rubble, blocking all access.  
If the rubble falls in a corridor, it blocks the width of the corridor. 

If it falls in a room or open space, it blocks an area 
1.5” radius centered on that location. 

Any figure within the blocked area can leap out of the way. 
89-00 Radiation build-up The area within 3” and Line of Sight of the Delve Hazard 

is radioactive. Any non-Sleeper/bot that begins or ends an 
activation in the area takes a Damage +0 hit, ignoring any 

existing Saving Throws. Instead, a special Saving Throw is 
allowed for scouts (5+) and scientists (4+).

Overpower If the creature also has a ranged attack, this applies to the ranged attack ONLY.

Ferocity This bonus does not apply if one of your characters moves to engage it.

158



Campaign Development

Lifeform Evolution table

D100 EVOLUTION DESCRIPTION

01-10 Enhanced Profile The creatures become more adapted to your specific combat methods. 

If the Lifeform would normally have a Combat Skill of +0, it is raised to 
+1. This includes reduced Combat Skills for Lifeforms capable of shooting.

Add +1” to Speed.
If the creature has a Strike Power of +0 damage, it is raised to +1.

11-20 Poison All of the creature’s attack forms apply a slow-acting nerve toxin.

Any character struck by the creature receives a Poison marker per hit. 
When the character activates, roll 1D6 for each Poison marker. If any of 

them result in a natural 6, the character becomes a casualty. If they do not, 
remove ONE Poison marker.

A scientist within 2” can attempt to help by spending their action and 
rolling 6+ on a 1D6+Savvy test. This removes one Poison marker.

21-30 Spines The creature becomes covered in sharp spikes.

Any character that loses a brawl against the creature takes 
an additional hit at +0 Damage. 

31-40 Duplication Through a psionic manifestation, the Lifeform is capable is reproducing 
spontaneously and immediately. 

At the start of each Enemy Phase, roll 1D6. If the roll is a 6, a random 
Lifeform duplicates. Place a second Lifeform adjacent to it. This ability does 

not activate if only Contacts are present on the table. 
41-50 Dramatic The creatures are changing rapidly in an unpredictable fashion

transformations Delete any Unique Ability the Lifeform lists on the Unique Abilities table 
(page 148). Instead, each battle where the creature is encountered, 

roll on the Unique Abilities table again and use the 
indicated ability during that battle.

51-60 Summoning The creatures emit a strange call that attracts more of them 
to the battlefield. 

At the start of each Enemy Phase, roll 1D6. If the roll is a 6, 
place a Contact on a random table edge.

This ability does not activate if no Contacts are present on the table.
61-70 Evasion Whether due to agility, chemical fog or psionic effects, the creatures 

are becoming difficult to target.

Each time a creature is fired upon, roll a D6. On a 6, it evades and is 
not hit. A creature that evades remains unable to be hit for the rest of the 

current battle round. If a creature evades in the Quick Actions Phase, 
it cannot attack when it activates in that Enemy Phase. 

Evading creatures can be hit by brawling attacks but cannot 
initiate it themselves.

159



Campaign Development

D100 EVOLUTION DESCRIPTION

71-80 Darts The Lifeform can now launch razor-tipped darts at nearby opponents.

Each creature will launch a dart at the end of its activation after all of its 
attacks and brawls have taken place. Darts have Range 9”, target the 

closest opponent visible, hit on a D6 roll of a 6, and inflict a 
Damage +0 hit. 

81-90 Bigger Leaders There are more pack leaders, and they are getting bigger as well.

The 4th Lifeform encountered in a mission is now a secondary leader with 
+1 KP. The 6th Lifeform encountered in a mission is a pack leader as 

usual. They receive +3 KP instead of the customary +2.
91-00 Tougher Specimens The creatures are getting bigger and meaner.

Each time a Lifeform is placed on the table, roll a D6. On 5-6. it has +1 KP.

D100 BREAKTHROUGH DESCRIPTION

01-10 Ancient Colony The remnants of ruins make it clear that this was once a colony, 
though whoever settled here has completely disappeared, leaving 
no traces of biological remains. Why they left is for the historians to 
decipher, but it is perhaps reassuring to know that others stood here 

before you and braved the same dangers.

Add 2 Ancient Sites to your map in random sectors.
This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you decide to pursue 

the Loyalty End Game.
11-20 Ancient Factory The world seems to have been intended as a site for a massive factory, 

though for what purpose remains unclear. The installations have long 
since decayed and only the shattered ruins remain. Artifacts found can 
provide tantalizing hints, not to mention valuable instructions for the 

researchers, but the truth may lie somewhere else entirely.

For the rest of the campaign, you receive 1 additional Build Point 
every campaign turn.

This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you pursue the 
Loyalty End Game.

169



Campaign Development

21-30 Artificial Construction Evidence increasingly points to the planet itself having been 
manufactured through unfathomable levels of technology. For what 

purpose is beyond your researchers to unravel, but it must have been 
grand to warrant such an expenditure of resources. 

Gain 3 Story Points and add 2 XP to three characters of your choice. 
This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you decide to pursue the 

Independence End Game.
31-40 Defense Network The planet bears signs of having been constructed, though by who 

is not clear. Evidently it was intended as part of a grand defensive 
network stretching across the stars, possibly to serve as a defensive 

perimeter against some expected invader on a galactic scale. 

Sleepers no longer receive a Saving Throw against your attacks. 
This Breakthrough provides a bonus if you pursue the 

Independence End Game.
41-50 Moved in Time or Space This is not the original location of this world, and it may not even be 

the original timeline either. The data is puzzling to say the least but, at 
some point, the cosmic fabric was manipulated on a scale that would 
transcend any such experiment currently understood to be possible.

Immediately obtain 10 Research Points.
This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you decide to pursue the 

Ascension End Game.

170



Campaign Development

51-60 Psionic Manipulation The world has been subjected to some of the largest psionic 
engineering ever witnessed. Its exact purpose is hazy at best and 

perhaps the very nature of the engineering prevents its secrets being 
unraveled. Clearly this will have a profound effect on 

future existence on this world. 

Select three characters on your roster and raise their 
Reaction scores by +1.

This Breakthrough provides a bonus if you pursue the 
Isolation End Game.

61-70 Semi-living Organism The entire planet appears to be a cohesive organism, the nature of 
which currently transcends our understanding. How such a creation 

could come to be is not easily explained, nor whether it did so 
naturally or through intelligent design. 

Reduce all current and future Hazard levels on the map by -1. 
This Breakthrough provides a bonus if you pursue the 

Isolation End Game.
71-80 Signs of Genetic It is becomes clear to you that the Lifeforms on this world are the result 

Modification of intentional genetic modification or have been created from scratch. 
The motive for doing so eludes you, but it raises important questions 

about the boundaries of life and your purpose in the universe. 

You immediately receive 5 Augmentation Points. 
This Breakthrough provides a bonus if you pursue the  

Ascension End Game.
81-90 Terraforming The world underwent massive terraforming efforts on a scale that is 

beyond our technological reach. There is little sign that long term 
colonization took place however, the ruins you find seemingly being 
abandoned quickly. Perhaps one day it will be clear why the colony 

was never completed, after such tremendous efforts. 

You may immediately add 10 Build Points.
This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you decide to pursue the 

Loyalty End Game.
91-00 Warzone The world bears the scars of a massive conflict fought here with 

weapons beyond our understanding. It is possible the damage you 
have uncovered may even stem from only stray shots originating in 

space. Whatever the conflict, those who waged it are no longer around 
to claim their victory or lament their defeat.

You may immediately add 4 grunts to your Colony Tracking Sheet. 
Add 3 Research Points. 

This Breakthrough also provides a bonus if you decide to pursue the 
Independence End Game.

171



Campaign Development

Prepare to embark on the grandest Five Parsecs adventure yet as you make planetfall 
on a world filled with wonders, terrors, and difficult challenges.

Planetfall is a solo and co-op adventure game where you take the role of a crew of colonists, 
scientists, and explorers from the mighty Unity of Humankind, building a colony on an alien 

world packed full of long-overgrown crashed starships and dangerous ancient ruins, 
while contending with mysterious and hostile lifeforms. 

You will have to direct your colony’s expansion and research as well as commanding 
your characters and troops in tactical miniatures combat. Over time, your colonists will gain 
experience and improve their combat abilities, while the R&D department adapts alien tech 

to upgrade your armories... and perhaps even your very bodies.
Stand-alone, compatible rules

The game is playable with any miniatures you would like to use and requires 
only a small figure count per battle. Rules are compatible with characters brought over 
from Five Parsecs From Home, Tactics, and Bug Hunt, allowing you to chain together 

the grandest space adventure you have ever experienced.
Features:

• Easy combat rules, allowing a single player to handle action quickly.
• Packed with random tables including artifacts, colony events, crises, and more.

• 14 mission types ranging from exploration to pitched battles to delves among alien ruins.
• Tactical enemies including pirates, renegades, outlaws, alien raiders, K’Erin landing parties,  

Converted recon teams... even hostile fellow colonists.
• In-depth research system with 13 scientific theories, 40 buildings, 

and 8 augmentations to unlock.
• As you explore, you will map out the world around your colony, and create your own unique 

encounter tables, filled with bizarre and evolving table-generated lifeforms.
• Assailants specific to the Kensington Reach setting: Introducing the psionic, saurian Slyn 

and ancient robot guardians, the Sleepers.
• Multiple epic endings possible for your colony. Printed in Lithuania
